</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ouarsenis_2012,_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/120px-Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/180px-Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/240px-Ouarsenis_2012%2C_Wilaya_de_Tissemsilt_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Ouarsenis" title="Ouarsenis">Ouarsenis</a>, range of mountains in North-Western (1985m)
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Les_Aiguades.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Les_Aiguades.jpg/120px-Les_Aiguades.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Les_Aiguades.jpg/180px-Les_Aiguades.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Les_Aiguades.jpg/240px-Les_Aiguades.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Maritime front of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beja%C3%AFa" title="Bejaïa">Bejaïa</a>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:35px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg/120px-Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg/180px-Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg/240px-Lagh-Algeria-SM.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Bakhdache valley <a href="/wiki/Laghouat" title="Laghouat">laghouat</a>.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Algeria is the largest country in Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>. Its southern part includes a significant portion of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. To the north, the <a href="/wiki/Tell_Atlas" title="Tell Atlas">Tell Atlas</a> form with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>, further south, two parallel sets of reliefs in approaching eastbound, and between which are inserted vast plains and highlands. Both Atlas tend to merge in eastern Algeria. The vast mountain ranges of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aures" title="Aures">Aures</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9bessa" title="Tébessa">Nememcha</a> occupy the entire northeastern Algeria and are delineated by the Tunisian border. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tahat" title="Mount Tahat">Mount Tahat</a> (3,003 m).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="624" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/220px-Algeria_relief.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/330px-Algeria_relief.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/440px-Algeria_relief.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahaggar_Mountains" title="Ahaggar Mountains">Ahaggar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas mountains</a> compose the Algerian relief.</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">19°</a> and <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a> (a small area is north of 37°N and south of 19°N), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_meridian_west" title="9th meridian west">9°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°E</a>. Most of the coastal area is hilly, sometimes even mountainous, and there are a few natural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbour" title="Harbour">harbours</a>. The area from the coast to the Tell Atlas is fertile. South of the Tell Atlas is a <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> landscape ending with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>; farther south, there is the Sahara desert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-75">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahaggar_Mountains" title="Ahaggar Mountains">Ahaggar Mountains</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">جبال هقار</span>‎), also known as the Hoggar, are a highland region in central Sahara, southern Algeria. They are located about 1,500 km (932 mi) south of the capital, Algiers, and just east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamanghasset" title="Tamanghasset">Tamanghasset</a>. Algiers, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> are Algeria's main cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-75">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_hydrology">Climate and hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate and hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Algeria" title="Climate of Algeria">Climate of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/300px-Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/450px-Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/600px-Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Algeria map of Köppen climate classification.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vue_de_Taghit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vue_de_Taghit.jpg/220px-Vue_de_Taghit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vue_de_Taghit.jpg/330px-Vue_de_Taghit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vue_de_Taghit.jpg/440px-Vue_de_Taghit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vue_de_Taghit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Saharan <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oasis</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Taghit" title="Taghit">Taghit</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agoulmime.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="612" data-file-width="960" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Agoulmime.jpg/220px-Agoulmime.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Agoulmime.jpg/330px-Agoulmime.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Agoulmime.jpg/440px-Agoulmime.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agoulmime.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lake Agoulmime, <a href="/wiki/Tikjda" title="Tikjda">Tikjda</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In this region, midday desert temperatures can be hot year round. After sunset, however, the clear, dry air permits rapid loss of heat, and the nights are cool to chilly. Enormous daily ranges in temperature are recorded.
</p><p>Rainfall is fairly plentiful along the coastal part of the Tell Atlas, ranging from 400 to 670 mm (15.7 to 26.4 in) annually, the amount of precipitation increasing from west to east. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is heaviest in the northern part of eastern Algeria, where it reaches as much as 1,000 mm (39.4 in) in some years.
</p><p>Farther inland, the rainfall is less plentiful. Algeria also has <a href="/wiki/Erg_(landform)" title="Erg (landform)">ergs</a>, or sand dunes, between mountains. Among these, in the summer time when winds are heavy and gusty, temperatures can get up to 43.3 °C (110 °F).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna_and_flora">Fauna and flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fauna and flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Algeria" title="Wildlife of Algeria">Wildlife of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_(Algeria).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="3264" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/220px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/330px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/440px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_(Algeria).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">Cedrus</a> of Chélia in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aures" title="Aures">Aures</a></div></div></div>
<p>The varied vegetation of Algeria includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal" title="Coastal">coastal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountainous" title="Mountainous">mountainous</a> and grassy <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>-like regions which all support a wide range of wildlife. Many of the creatures comprising the Algerian wildlife live in close proximity to civilization. The most commonly seen animals include the wild <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boar" title="Boar">boars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackal" title="Jackal">jackals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a>, although it is not uncommon to spot <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fennecs" title="Fennecs">fennecs</a> (foxes), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerboas" title="Jerboas">jerboas</a>. Algeria also has a small <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopard</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saharan_cheetah" title="Saharan cheetah">Saharan cheetah</a> population, but these are seldom seen. A species of deer, the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_stag" title="Barbary stag">Barbary stag</a>, inhabits the dense humid forests in the north-eastern areas.
</p><p>A variety of bird species makes the country an attraction for bird watchers. The forests are inhabited by boars and jackals. <a href="/wiki/Barbary_macaque" title="Barbary macaque">Barbary macaques</a> are the sole native monkey. Snakes, <a href="/wiki/Monitor_lizard" title="Monitor lizard">monitor lizards</a>, and numerous other reptiles can be found living among an array of <a href="/wiki/Rodent" title="Rodent">rodents</a> throughout the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi_arid" title="Semi arid">semi arid</a> regions of Algeria. Many animals are now extinct, including the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_lion" title="Barbary lion">Barbary lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_bear" title="Atlas bear">Atlas bears</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_African_crocodile" title="West African crocodile">crocodiles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the north, some of the native flora includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macchia" title="Macchia">Macchia</a> scrub, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olive trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">cedars</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">conifers</a>. The mountain regions contain large forests of evergreens (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleppo_pine" title="Aleppo pine">Aleppo pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergreen_oak" title="Evergreen oak">evergreen oak</a>) and some deciduous trees. <a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">Fig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agave" title="Agave">agave</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palm trees</a> grow in the warmer areas. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grape_vine" title="Grape vine">grape vine</a> is indigenous to the coast. In the Sahara region, some oases have palm trees. <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">Acacias</a> with wild <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> are the predominant flora in the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">Camels</a> are used extensively; the desert also abounds with venomous and nonvenomous snakes, <a href="/wiki/Scorpion" title="Scorpion">scorpions</a>, and numerous insects.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Algeria" title="Politics of Algeria">Politics of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2720" data-file-width="4080" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/220px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/330px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/440px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1421" data-file-width="913" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG/150px-President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG/225px-President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG/300px-President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President-abdelaziz-bouteflika.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_President" title="Algerian President">Algerian President</a> Abdelaziz Bouteflika</div></div></div>
<p>Elected politicians are considered to have relatively little sway over Algeria. Instead, a group of unelected civilian and military "décideurs", known as "le pouvoir" ("the power"), actually rule the country, even deciding who should be president. The most powerful man may be <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Medi%C3%A8ne" title="Mohamed Mediène">Mohamed Mediène</a>, head of the military intelligence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> In recent years, many of these generals have died or retired. After the death of General <a href="/wiki/Larbi_Belkheir" title="Larbi Belkheir">Larbi Belkheir</a>, Bouteflika put loyalists in key posts, notably at <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, and secured constitutional amendments that make him re-electable indefinitely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>The head of state is the president of Algeria, who is elected for a five-year term. The president was formerly limited to two five-year terms, but a constitutional amendment passed by the Parliament on 11 November 2008 removed this limitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Algeria has universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> at 18 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> The President is the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_Army" title="Algerian Army">army</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Algeria" title="Council of Ministers of Algeria">Council of Ministers</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=High_Security_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="High Security Council (page does not exist)">High Security Council</a>. He appoints the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Algeria" title="Prime Minister of Algeria">Prime Minister</a> who is also the head of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-president_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-president-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Algerian parliament is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a>; the lower house, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a>, has 462 members who are directly elected for five-year terms, while the upper house, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Nation" title="Council of the Nation">Council of the Nation</a>, has 144 members serving six-year terms, of which 96 members are chosen by local assemblies and 48 are appointed by the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitw13_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-81">[80]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Algeria" title="Constitution of Algeria">constitution</a>, no political association may be formed if it is "based on differences in religion, language, race, gender, profession, or region". In addition, political campaigns must be exempt from the aforementioned subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Parliamentary elections were last held in <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_2012" title="Algerian legislative election, 2012">May 2012</a>, and were judged to be largely free by international monitors, though local groups alleged fraud and irregularities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitw13_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-81">[80]</a></sup> In the elections, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Front (Algeria)">FLN</a> won 221 seats, the military-backed <a href="/wiki/National_Rally_for_Democracy_(Algeria)" title="National Rally for Democracy (Algeria)">National Rally for Democracy</a> won 70, and the Islamist <a href="/wiki/Green_Algeria_Alliance" title="Green Algeria Alliance">Green Algeria Alliance</a> won 47.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitw13_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Algeria" title="Foreign relations of Algeria">Foreign relations of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="514" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/220px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/330px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/440px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> exchange handshakes at the Windsor Hotel Toya Resort and Spa in Tōyako Town, Abuta District, Hokkaidō in 2008. With them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dmitriy_Medvedev" title="Dmitriy Medvedev">Dmitriy Medvedev</a>, left, and <a href="/wiki/Yasuo_Fukuda" title="Yasuo Fukuda">Yasuo Fukuda</a>, right.</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria is included in the European Union's <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer.
Giving incentives and rewarding best performers, as well as offering funds in a faster and more flexible manner, are the two main principles underlying the European Neighbourhood Instrument (ENI) that came into force in 2014. It has a budget of €15.4 billion and provides the bulk of funding through a number of programmes.
</p><p>In 2009, the French government agreed to compensate victims of nuclear tests in Algeria. Defense Minister Herve Morin stated that "It's time for our country to be at peace with itself, at peace thanks to a system of compensation and reparations," when presenting the draft law on the payouts. Algerian officials and activists believe that this is a good first step and hope that this move would encourage broader reparation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tensions between Algeria and Morocco in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> have been an obstacle to tightening the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a>, nominally established in 1989, but which has carried little practical weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Algeria" title="Military of Algeria">Military of Algeria</a></div>
<p>The military of Algeria consists of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Army" title="People's National Army">People's National Army</a> (ANP), the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_National_Navy" title="Algerian National Navy">Algerian National Navy</a> (MRA), and the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Air_Force" title="Algerian Air Force">Algerian Air Force</a> (QJJ), plus the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Air_Defence_Forces" title="Territorial Air Defence Forces">Territorial Air Defence Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> It is the direct successor of the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Army (Algeria)">National Liberation Army</a> (Armée de Libération Nationale or ALN), the armed wing of the nationalist National Liberation Front which fought French colonial <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a> during the Algerian War of Independence (1954–62).
</p><p>Total military personnel include 147,000 active, 150,000 reserve, and 187,000 paramilitary staff (2008 estimate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IISS_TMB_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-IISS_TMB-85">[84]</a></sup> Service in the military is compulsory for men aged 19–30, for a total of 12 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> The military expenditure was 4.3% of the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">second largest military</a> in North Africa with the largest defence budget in Africa ($10 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaSpending_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaSpending-13">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, the Algerian Air Force signed a deal with Russia to purchase 49 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">MiG-29</a>SMT and 6 MiG-29UBT at an estimated cost of $1.9 billion. Russia is also building two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilo_class_submarine" title="Kilo class submarine">636-type</a> diesel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Submarines" title="Submarines">submarines</a> for Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Algeria" title="Human rights in Algeria">Human rights in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Algeria has been categorized by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> as "not free" since it began publishing such ratings in 1972, with the exception of 1989, 1990, and 1991, when the country was labeled "partly free."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> In December 2016, the <i>Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor</i> issued a report regarding violation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_freedom" title="Media freedom">media freedom</a> in Algeria. It clarified that the Algerian government imposed restriction on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>; expression; and right to peaceful demonstration, protest and assembly as well as intensified censorship of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_media" title="Broadcast media">media</a> and websites. Due to the fact that the journalists and activists criticize the ruling government, some media organizations' licenses are canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>Independent and autonomous trade unions face routine harassment from the government, with many leaders imprisoned and protests suppressed. In 2016 a number of unions, many of which were involved in the 2010–2012 Algerian Protests, have been deregistered by the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Algeria" title="LGBT rights in Algeria">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Public homosexual behavior is punishable by up to two years in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">Provinces of Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">Districts of Algeria</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" title="Municipalities of Algeria">Municipalities of Algeria</a></div>
<p>Algeria is divided into 48 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">provinces</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilaya" title="Wilaya">wilayas</a></i>), 553 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">districts</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Da%C3%AFra" title="Daïra">daïras</a></i>) and 1,541 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" title="Municipalities of Algeria">municipalities</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Baladiyah" title="Baladiyah">baladiyahs</a></i>). Each province, district, and municipality is named after its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">seat</a>, which is usually the largest city.
</p><p>The administrative divisions have changed several times since independence. When introducing new provinces, the numbers of old provinces are kept, hence the non-alphabetical order. With their official numbers, currently (since 1983) they are<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Algeria" title="Economy of Algeria">Economy of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="863" data-file-width="1102" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/250px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/375px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/500px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of the country's exports in 28 colour-coded categories.</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria is classified as an upper middle income country by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> Algeria's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_dinar" title="Algerian dinar">dinar</a> (DZD). The economy remains dominated by the state, a legacy of the country's socialist post-independence development model. In recent years, the Algerian government has halted the privatization of state-owned industries and imposed restrictions on imports and foreign involvement in its economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> These restrictions are just started to be lifted off recently although questions about Algeria's slow diversifying economy remains.
</p><p>Algeria has struggled to develop industries outside hydrocarbons in part because of high costs and an inert state bureaucracy. The government's efforts to diversify the economy by attracting foreign and domestic investment outside the energy sector have done little to reduce high youth unemployment rates or to address housing shortages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> The country is facing a number of short-term and medium-term problems, including the need to diversify the economy, strengthen political, economic and financial reforms, improve the business climate and reduce inequalities amongst regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>A wave of economic protests in February and March 2011 prompted the Algerian government to offer more than $23 billion in public grants and retroactive salary and benefit increases. Public spending has increased by 27% annually during the past 5 years. The 2010–14 public-investment programme will cost US$286 billion, 40% of which will go to human development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Theatre_d%27oran.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/220px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/330px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/440px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Theatre_d%27oran.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The port city of Oran</div></div></div>
<p>The Algerian economy grew by 2.6% in 2011, driven by public spending, in particular in the construction and public-works sector, and by growing internal demand. If hydrocarbons are excluded, growth has been estimated at 4.8%. Growth of 3% is expected in 2012, rising to 4.2% in 2013. The rate of inflation was 4% and the budget deficit 3% of GDP. The current-account surplus is estimated at 9.3% of GDP and at the end of December 2011, official reserves were put at US$182 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup> Inflation, the lowest in the region, has remained stable at 4% on average between 2003 and 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MFW4A_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-MFW4A-96">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="272" data-file-width="442" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/250px-Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/375px-Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Algeria, trends in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> 1970–2010</div></div></div>
<p>In 2011 Algeria announced a budgetary surplus of $26.9 billion, 62% increase in comparison to 2010 surplus. In general, the country exported $73 billion worth of commodities while it imported $46 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thanks to strong hydrocarbon revenues, Algeria has a cushion of $173 billion in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_currency_reserves" title="Foreign currency reserves">foreign currency reserves</a> and a large hydrocarbon stabilization fund. In addition, Algeria's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_external_debt" title="List of countries by external debt">external debt</a> is extremely low at about 2% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> The economy remains very dependent on hydrocarbon wealth, and, despite high foreign exchange reserves (US$178 billion, equivalent to three years of imports), current expenditure growth makes Algeria's budget more vulnerable to the risk of prolonged lower hydrocarbon revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-98">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the agricultural sector and services recorded growth of 10% and 5.3%, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup> About 14% of the labor force are employed in the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Algeria" title="Agriculture in Algeria">agricultural sector</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> Fiscal policy in 2011 remained expansionist and made it possible to maintain the pace of public investment and to contain the strong demand for jobs and housing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-5"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria has not joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO" title="WTO">WTO</a>, despite several years of negotiations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2006, Russia agreed to erase $4.74 billion of Algeria's <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a>-era debt<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> during a visit by <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> to the country, the first by a Russian leader in half a century. In return, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Algeria" title="President of Algeria">Algerian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> agreed to buy $7.5 billion worth of combat planes, air-defence systems and other arms from Russia, according to the head of Russia's state arms exporter <a href="/wiki/Rosoboronexport" title="Rosoboronexport">Rosoboronexport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Dubai-based conglomerate Emarat Dzayer Group said it had signed a joint venture agreement to develop a $1.6 billion steel factory in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrocarbons">Hydrocarbons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hydrocarbons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Algeria" title="Mining industry of Algeria">Mining industry of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="832" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/220px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/330px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/440px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pipelines across Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria, whose economy is reliant on petroleum, has been an <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> member since 1969. Its crude oil production stands at around 1.1 million barrels/day, but it is also a major gas producer and exporter, with important links to Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opb15_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-opb15-104">[103]</a></sup> Hydrocarbons have long been the backbone of the economy, accounting for roughly 60% of budget revenues, 30% of GDP, and over 95% of export earnings. Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">10th-largest reserves of natural gas</a> in the world and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">sixth-largest gas exporter</a>. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a> reported that in 2005, Algeria had 160 trillion cubic feet (4.5<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>12</sup> m<sup>3</sup>) of proven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves" title="Natural gas reserves">natural-gas reserves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciawfb_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-ciawfb-105">[104]</a></sup> It also ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">16th in oil reserves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Non-hydrocarbon growth for 2011 was projected at 5%. To cope with social demands, the authorities raised expenditure, especially on basic food support, employment creation, support for SMEs, and higher salaries. High hydrocarbon prices have improved the current account and the already large international reserves position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-98">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>Income from oil and gas rose in 2011 as a result of continuing high oil prices, though the trend in production volume is downwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-6"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup> Production from the oil and gas sector in terms of volume, continues to decline, dropping from 43.2 million tonnes to 32 million tonnes between 2007 and 2011. Nevertheless, the sector accounted for 98% of the total volume of exports in 2011, against 48% in 1962,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> and 70% of budgetary receipts, or USD 71.4 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-7"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Algerian national oil company is <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, which plays a key role in all aspects of the oil and natural gas sectors in Algeria. All foreign operators must work in partnership with Sonatrach, which usually has majority ownership in production-sharing agreements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_alternative_energy_sources">Research and alternative energy sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Research and alternative energy sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Algeria has invested an estimated 100 billion dinars towards developing research facilities and paying researchers. This development program is meant to advance alternative energy production, especially solar and wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Algeria is estimated to have the largest solar energy potential in the Mediterranean, so the government has funded the creation of a solar science park in Hassi R'Mel. Currently, Algeria has 20,000 research professors at various universities and over 780 research labs, with state-set goals to expand to 1,000. Besides solar energy, areas of research in Algeria include space and satellite telecommunications, nuclear power and medical research.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Labour market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite a decline in total <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, youth and women unemployment is high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-98">[97]</a></sup> Unemployment particularly affects the young, with a jobless rate of 21.5% among the 15–24 age group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-8"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>The overall rate of unemployment was 10% in 2011, but remained higher among young people, with a rate of 21.5% for those aged between 15 and 24. The government strengthened in 2011 the job programmes introduced in 1988, in particular in the framework of the programme to aid those seeking work (Dispositif d'Aide à l'Insertion Professionnelle).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_74-9"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Algeria" title="Tourism in Algeria">Tourism in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2981" data-file-width="4500" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/220px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/330px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/440px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Djanet" title="Djanet">Djanet</a></div></div></div>
<p>The development of the tourism sector in Algeria had previously been hampered by a lack of facilities, but since 2004 a broad tourism development strategy has been implemented resulting in many hotels of a high modern standard being built.
</p><p>There are several <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> in Algeria<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Qal%27a_of_Beni_Hammad" title="Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad">Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad</a>, the first capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammadid" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a> empire; <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>, a Phoenician and later Roman town; and <a href="/wiki/Dj%C3%A9mila" title="Djémila">Djémila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timgad" title="Timgad">Timgad</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> ruins; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%27Zab_Valley" title="M'Zab Valley">M'Zab Valley</a>, a limestone valley containing a large urbanized <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oasis</a>; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casbah" title="Casbah">Casbah</a> of Algiers, an important citadel. The only natural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Tassili_n%27Ajjer" title="Tassili n'Ajjer">Tassili n'Ajjer</a>, a mountain range.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Algeria" title="Transport in Algeria">Transport in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1528" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/220px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/330px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/440px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main highway connecting the Moroccan to the Tunisian border was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Cairo%E2%80%93Dakar_Highway" title="Cairo–Dakar Highway">Cairo–Dakar Highway</a> project</div></div></div>
<p>The Algerian road network is the densest in Africa; its length is estimated at 180,000 km of highways, with more than 3,756 structures and a paving rate of 85%. This network will be complemented by the <a href="/wiki/Algeria_East%E2%80%93West_Highway" title="Algeria East–West Highway">East-West Highway</a>, a major infrastructure project currently under construction. It is a 3-way, 1,216-kilometre-long (756 mi) highway, linking <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> in the extreme east to the <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a> in the far west. Algeria is also crossed by the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Sahara_Highway" title="Trans-Sahara Highway">Trans-Sahara Highway</a>, which is now completely paved. This road is supported by the Algerian government to increase trade between the six countries crossed: Algeria, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Algeria" title="Demographics of Algeria">Demographics of Algeria</a></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:170px;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="text-align:right;padding:1px">8,615</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.70%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1966 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">12,022</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+2.82%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1977 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">16,948</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+3.17%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1987 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">23,051</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+3.12%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1998 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">29,113</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.15%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2008 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">34,080</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.59%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2013 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">37,900</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.15%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: (1856–1872)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kateb2001_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kateb2001-110">[109]</a></sup> (1886–2008)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rgp08p82_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-rgp08p82-111">[110]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Algerien_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2016 Algeria's population was an estimated 40.4 million, who are mainly <a href="/wiki/Arab-Berber" title="Arab-Berber">Arab-Berber</a> ethnically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-12"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ons_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-ons-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ber_evidance_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ber_evidance-113">[112]</a></sup> At the outset of the 20th century, its population was approximately four million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> About 90% of Algerians live in the northern, coastal area; the inhabitants of the Sahara desert are mainly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a>, although some 1.5 million remain <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> or partly nomadic. 28.1% of Algerians are under the age of 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-13"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Women make up 70% of the country's lawyers and 60% of its judges and also dominate the field of medicine. Increasingly, women are contributing more to household income than men. 60% of university students are women, according to university researchers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 90,000 and 165,000 <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawis</a> from Western Sahara live in the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps" title="Sahrawi refugee camps">Sahrawi refugee camps</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-116">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-117">[116]</a></sup> in the western Algerian Sahara desert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> There are also more than 4,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" title="Palestinian refugee">Palestinian refugees</a>, who are well integrated and have not asked for assistance from the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-116">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-117">[116]</a></sup> In 2009, 35,000 <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> migrant workers lived in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest concentration of Algerian migrants outside Algeria is in France, which has reportedly over 1.7 million Algerians of up to the second generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Algeria" title="Ethnic groups in Algeria">Ethnic groups in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greeks" title="Byzantine Greeks">Byzantines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africans" title="Sub-Saharan Africans">Sub-Saharan Africans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> have contributed to the history of Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Descendants of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Andalusian</a> refugees are also present in the population of Algiers and other cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> was spoken by these <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragonese</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castilian_people" title="Castilian people">Castillian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moriscos" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants deep into the 18th century, and even <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> was spoken at the same time by <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moriscos" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants in the small town of Grish El-Oued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="460" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/220px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/330px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/440px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some of Algeria's traditional clothes</div></div></div>
<p>Despite the dominance of the Berber culture and ethnicity in Algeria, the majority of Algerians identify with an Arabic-based identity, especially after the Arab nationalism rising in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> Berbers and Berber-speaking Algerians are divided into many groups with varying languages. The largest of these are the Kabyles, who live in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a> region east of Algiers, the Chaoui of Northeast Algeria, the Tuaregs in the southern desert and the <a href="/wiki/Chenouas" title="Chenouas">Shenwa people</a> of North Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>During the colonial period, there was a large (10% in 1960)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cook_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-127">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> population who became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a></i>. They were primarily of French, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> origin. Almost all of this population left during the war of independence or immediately after its end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Algeria" title="Languages of Algeria">Languages of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Algeria" title="French language in Algeria">French language in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/220px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/330px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/440px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Signs in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Tizi_Ouzou" title="University of Tizi Ouzou">University of Tizi Ouzou</a> in three languages: <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>, and French</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_language" title="Berber language">Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> are the official languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> (Darja) is the language used by the majority of the population. Colloquial Algerian Arabic is heavily infused with borrowings from French and Berber.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_language" title="Berber language">Berber</a> has been recognized as a "national language" by the constitutional amendment of 8 May 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">Kabyle</a>, the predominant Berber language, is taught and is partially co-official (with a few restrictions) in parts of <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a>. In February 2016, the Algerian constitution passed a resolution that would make Berber an official language alongside Arabic.
</p><p>Although <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> has no official status, Algeria is the second-largest Francophone country in the world in terms of speakers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> and French is widely used in government, media (newspapers, radio, local television), and both the education system (from primary school onwards) and academia due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_rule_in_Algeria" title="French rule in Algeria">Algeria's colonial history</a>. It can be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of Algeria. In 2008, 11.2 million Algerians could read and write in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> An Abassa Institute study in April 2000 found that 60% of households could speak and understand French or 18 million in a population of 30 million then. After an earlier period during which the Algerian government tried to phase out French (which is why it has no official status), in recent decades the government has backtracked and reinforced the study of French and TV programs have reinforced use of the language.
</p><p>Algeria emerged as a bilingual state after 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> Colloquial <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> is spoken by about 72% of the population and Berber by 27–30%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leclerc_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-leclerc-134">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Algeria" title="Religion in Algeria">Religion in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_African_Church" title="Early African Church">Early African Church</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Algeria" title="History of the Jews in Algeria">History of the Jews in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg/220px-Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg/330px-Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg/440px-Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Djama%C3%A2_el_Kebir.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Algiers" title="Great Mosque of Algiers">Great Mosque of Algiers</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Islam is the predominant religion in Algeria, with its adherents, mostly Sunnis, accounting for 99% of the population according to a 2012 CIA World Factbook estimate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_5-14"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> and 97.9% according to Pew Research in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-pew-135">[134]</a></sup> There are about 150,000 <a href="/wiki/Ibadi" title="Ibadi">Ibadis</a> in the M'zab Valley in the region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghardaia" title="Ghardaia">Ghardaia</a>.
</p><p>Algeria has given the Muslim world a number of prominent thinkers, including <a href="/wiki/Emir_Abdelkader" title="Emir Abdelkader">Emir Abdelkader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Ben_Badis" title="Abdelhamid Ben Badis">Abdelhamid Ben Badis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Kacem_Na%C3%AEt_Belkacem" title="Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem">Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohamed_Arkoun" title="Mohamed Arkoun">Mohamed Arkoun</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Algeria" title="List of cities in Algeria">List of cities in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Below is a list of the most important Algerian cities:
